INTRODUCTION
The Marathon Oil Company, Kary 11-17H [NW NW Section 17, T144N, R96W] is located
approximately 7 miles northwest of Manning in Dunn County, North Dakota (Figure 1). The
well is a single lateral, double section horizontal well that's part of a multi-well pad, and has a
target pay zone in the Mississippian-Devonian Middle Bakken Member. The Middle Bakken is a
mixed carbonate-clastic sequence stratigraphically located between two petroliferous &
carbonaceous black shale members, the upper Bakken shale and the lower Bakken shale. The
two shale members serve as the prospects source rock.
PLAN
The drilling plan stipulated that the vertical hole inclination should be held at an inclination of
3.00º with an azimuth of 335° from surface casing at 2,336' MD until approximately 10,344'
MD, where the curve would be kicked-off for a 12º per 100' build until landing at approximately
11,171' MD (10,886' TVD) in the target. Prognosis estimated the landing target to be 15' below
the base of the upper Bakken shale. After landing, intermediate casing would then be set and
cemented to isolate the target reservoir, and the lateral would commence. The lateral would
continue north at approximately 180º to a bottom hole location within SW SW, Section 20,
T144N-R96W.
OFFSET WELLS
Top and thickness control was provided by three main offsets (Figure 2). The following offset
wells provided gamma signatures to correlate formation tops; allowing thickness evaluation for a
proper target landing, and provided gamma signature and structure control during lateral
operations. The three offsets include:
The Marathon Oil Company Louie Hendricks 24-20H, which is located approximately
2 miles south-southwest of the subject well. It is a horizontal, Middle Bakken well
drilled in June of 2009. The horizontal path parallels the path of the Kary 11-17H, so
this offset will be used to compare structure and gamma.
The Davis Oil Co. Murphy Creek State 1 is located approximately 1.3 miles east of the
Kary 11-17H, and was completed in December of 1983. The Murphy Creek State 1
was a vertical hole drilled down to the Duperow Formation, and is classified as a dry
hole. This offset is used to encapsulate the entire Middle Bakken gamma signature.
The Marathon Oil Company Piatt 11-17H is located on the same pad of the subject
well, with a vertical-curve section drilled prior to the subject well. It was used as the
primary offset for landing operations.
Figure 2. Map showing the location of the Marathon Oil Company, Kary 11-17H and the location of the three
wells used for offset control.
ENGINEERING
The well was spud by rig Ensign #161 on September 11, 2014. Surface casing was set using 9
5/8" 36 pound J-55 casing, and isolated the surface hole to 2,336' MD. The remaining vertical
hole was drilled with diesel invert drilling fluid with a weight of 9.6 to 10.6 pounds/gallon. The
vertical was drilled with two assemblies to kick-off point at 10,346'MD.
The curve kicked off at 10,346' MD, using a 2.12° mud motor, and was completed at 11,248'
MD (10,881' TVD). The curve was drilled in approximately 18 hours using a single assembly.
After completing the curve section of the well, 7" casing was set and cemented to 11,233' MD,
using 32# P-110 casing.
In preparation for drilling the lateral portion of the well, invert diesel drilling fluid was displaced
with salt water drilling fluid. The lateral commenced on November 21st, 2014, using a single
assembly, consisting of a 6" PDC bit and BHI XLP motor, to drill the lateral section from
11,248' MD to total depth at 22,880' in 56.5 hours.
The Kary 11-17H reached total depth of 21,880' on November 24th, 2014, at a closure direction
of 178.54° and a true vertical depth (TVD) of 10,846'. The bottom hole location was estimated
to be 9,973.32' south and 254.09' east of the surface location or approximately 226.15' FSL &
1,305.095' FWL, SE SW Section 20, T144N, R96W (Figure 3).

GEOLOGIC EVALUATION
Methods
A two-person geology team logged drill cuttings, monitored mud gas and provided guidance for
steering. Sample and gas evaluation began in the Kibbey Formation at 8,670' MD. Rig crew
members caught 30' lagged samples under direction of the well-site geologists. Wet and dry
cuttings were examined under a binocular microscope. Two sets of dry cuttings were collected
and sent to Marathon Oil Company and the North Dakota Geological Survey. A digital gas
detector (total gas with chromatograph) was interfaced with a Pason electronic data recorder
(EDR). The Pason EDR provided hole depth, bit depth and pump stroke information to the gas
detection program (MController) and distributed the detector's total gas information for viewing
across location. Total mud gas was recorded in units (100 units = 1% methane equivalent in air)
and chromatography of C1 ­ C4 components were calculated in parts-per-million.
Lithology
Note: There were no electric logs run for the Kary 11-17H; therefore, all depths while drilling the vertical and
curve are referenced to driller's depth.
Beginning in the Mississippian, Kibbey Formation of the Big Snowy Group, sample collection
and logging continued into the Mississippian-Devonian Middle Bakken Member. The Bakken
Formation is the only strata discussed in detail here, complete sample descriptions by depth can
be found in an addendum to this report.
The Bakken Formation, Upper Bakken Shale Member was penetrated at 10,855' TVD (-8,734'
MSL). This member is easily recognized by a sharp increase and sustained high gamma ray
counts, a marked increase in penetration rates, typically sustained higher gas shows and distinct
sample changes. The upper shale is a black, carbonaceous & petroliferous shale containing
occasional to common disseminated and nodular pyrite (Figure 4). The Middle Bakken Member
was penetrated at 10,867' TVD (-8,446' MSL). The middle Bakken consists of a light to medium
gray-brown silty sandstone, containing fine intergranular porosity and light brown, spotty oil
staining (Figure 5). The top for this member was picked from a combination of decreased
gamma counts, decreased total gas, a decrease in penetration rates and sample changes.
Figures 4 & 5: Wet cuttings of Upper Bakken shale (left), and Middle Bakken silty sandstone (right).
Geosteering
The well prognosis called for a landing target 15' into the Middle Bakken Member, at a depth of
10,886' TVD. Using gamma signatures from offset wells, well-site geologists were able to
correlate formation tops in order to make necessary corrections to the prognosis landing target.
Lodgepole markers came in consistently high to prognosis, and the decision was made to raise
the landing target a total of 4' to 10,882' TVD. The actual curve landing came in at 10,881'
TVD, landing the well-bore 1' into the 8' geologic window.
Three primary gamma signatures were used to steer the well in the 8' thick geologic window.
Throughout our target interval, gamma counts ranged from roughly 45-100 (API), and oscillated
with regularity. This gamma trend was pervasive throughout our entire zone which proposed a
challenge determining our precise location within the target. The two other markers used to steer
the well were observed above and below our target zone. Above the zone, a reliable packestone
marker was observed. Gamma counts in this packestone layer cooled down considerably to
around 20-30 (API). This packestone layer was easily distinguish in sample due to a much lighter
coloration when compared to samples from other intervals within the Middle Bakken Member.
Ooids were also observed in this packestone layer, which differentiated it from our target zone.
At the bottom of our target interval, a hotter and tighter gamma marker was observed with API
counts of 75-100. This marker bounded our target zone below and was encountered several times
throughout the lateral portion of the well. These markers provided data upon which formation
dip was calculated, and were consistent throughout the lateral.
The target window was entered at approximately 11,180' MD, and the well-bore was maintained
in the target for approximately 79% of the lateral. Over the course of the 10,080' lateral, the
center line of our target dropped a total of 33.10' TVD, resulting in a gross apparent dip of
+0.19° (Figure 6).

Hydrocarbons
Gas shows increased towards the bottom of the Lodgepole Formation. Several gas shows of
between 3,000 to 4,000 units were observed while drilling the curve through the lower
Lodgepole Formation. These shows can most likely be attributed to high hydrocarbon content in
the Upper Bakken Shale Member, as well as zones of possible fracture porosity towards the
bottom of the Lodgepole Formation.
Background gas throughout the lateral ranged from 150 to 3,100 units, with an average of around
1,400 units (Figure 7). Several intervals of the lateral produced notable increases in background
gas and gas shows. The highest gas shows were observed within our target window, however
apart from this observation, there is little evidence to link high gas shows to a particular portion
of our drilling window. Observed increases are likely a result of localized zones of high pressure
and/or porosity. Oil was observed coming over the shakers early in the lateral, changing from
light brown to greenish brown to green as the lateral progressed. Spotty brown oil staining was
observed in sample for the entire duration of the lateral, and cuts of samples yielded primarily
fast streaming yellow-green to blue cut fluorescence.
Gas was vented through the gas buster beginning at 12,500' MD, and circulated through the gas
buster beginning at 14,900' MD, and continued throughout the remainder of the lateral. A 3-5'
intermittent flare was observed beginning around 13,500' MD, increasing to a 5-10' intermittent
flare around 16,000' MD through total depth. No back-pressure was held during the lateral. Gas
values increased notably after total depth while liner was run, with gas shows over 8,000 units
and 30-40' flares.

SUMMARY
The Kary 11-17H was drilled in 15 days, eventually reaching total depth of 20,880' MD on
November 24th, 2014.
The well exposed 9,700' of the Middle Bakken Member, and was
determined to be 79% within the target interval. The target zone contained silty sandstone,
containing fine intergranular porosity and spotty, light brown oil staining. An overall dip of
+0.19° was calculated using a combination of gamma ray, sample analysis, and drilling
parameter data. Despite the challenges presented by the lack of reliable gamma markers directly
within our target interval and a relatively thin Middle Bakken interval, the Kary 11-17H proved
to be an engineering and geologic success. Sample analyses combined with gas data provide
strong evidence that the Kary 11-17H will be a successful Bakken well. The well currently
awaits fracture stimulation to maximize its potential as an oil and gas well.
Respectfully submitted,
Nathan Stansfield
Anna Bruckmeier
Sunburst Consulting, Inc.
November 30th, 2014

LITHOLOGY
Marathon Oil Company ­ Kary 11-17H
Rig crews caught lagged samples in 30' intervals under the supervision of Sunburst geologists. A detailed
list of sampling intervals is included in the well data summary page. Sample or gamma ray marker tops
have been inserted in the sample descriptions below for reference. Samples were examined wet and dry
under a binocular microscope. The drilling fluid was diesel based invert from surface casing to 11,248'
and changed to salt-water from 11,248' to 20,880' (TD). Sample collection began at 8,670'.
Drilling in the Kibbey Formation
8650-8670 SILTSTONE: red to brown, occasional red to orange, firm to friable, sub-blocky to blocky, calcite
cemented, poorly cemented; trace ANHYDRITE: off white to cream, microcrystalline, soft, amorphous
8670-8700 SILTY SANDSTONE: light to medium brown, red-orange, firm to friable, very fine grained, calcite
cemented, moderately well cemented
8700-8730 SILTSTONE: red to brown, occasional red to orange, firm to friable, sub-blocky to blocky, calcite
cemented, poorly cemented; trace ANHYDRITE: off white to cream, microcrystalline, soft, amorphous
Kibbey "Lime"
8,755' MD; 8,748' TVD (-6,327')
8730-8760 LIMESTONE: mudstone, light to medium gray, friable to firm, earthy texture, trace ANHYDRITE:
cream to light brown, microcrystalline, amorphous; trace SILTSTONE: red to red-brown, soft to friable, blocky,
calcite cemented, poorly cemented
8760-8790 SILTSTONE: red to brown, trace red to orange, firm, sub-blocky, calcite cemented, sandy in part, poorly
cemented
8790-8820 SILTSTONE: red to brown, trace red to orange, firm, sub-blocky, calcite cemented, sandy in part, poorly
cemented
8820-8850 SILTSTONE: red to brown, trace red to orange, firm, sub-blocky, calcite cemented, sandy in part, poorly
cemented
8850-8880 SILTSTONE: red to brown, trace red to orange, firm, sub-blocky, calcite cemented, sandy in part, poorly
cemented; trace LIMESTONE: mudstone, light gray-brown, microcrystalline, firm to friable, earthy texture;
occasional ANHYDRITE: white to cream, soft, amorphous
8880-8910 SILTSTONE: red to brown, trace red to orange, firm, sub-blocky, calcite cemented, sandy in part, poorly
cemented; trace LIMESTONE: mudstone, light gray-brown, microcrystalline, firm to friable, earthy texture;

HORIZONTAL WELL
KARY 11-17H
NWNW Section 17-144N-96W

Well File # 28663
Dear Natalie:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 22900, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The
approval is granted on the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement, be no closer than
the 200' setback from the north & south boundaries and 500' setback from the east & west boundaries within the
1280 acre spacing unit consisting of Sections 17& 20 T144N R96W.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: Effective June 1, 2014, a covered leak-proof container (with placard) for
filter sock disposal must be maintained on the well site beginning when the well is spud, and must
remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations are
conducted. MARATHON OIL COMPANY must run open hole logs to include a porosity and
resistivity log from KOP to the base of the surface casing. Marathon may set conductor on permitted
wells only. MARATHON OIL CO must contact NDIC Field Inspector Nicole Nelson at 701-290-1527
prior to location construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well
drilling and completion operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will
prevent pollution of the land surface and freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits
are prohibited. All pits shall be inspected by an authorized representative of the director prior to lining and use.
Drill cuttings and solids must be stabilized in a manner approved by the director prior to placement in a cuttings
pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC.
The proposed directional plan is at a legal location. Based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum
legal coordinate from the well head is: 10003 S.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the
approved drilling permit on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to
commence before the 3rd business day following publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may
be waived by the Director. Application for a waiver must be by sworn affidavit providing the information
necessary to evaluate the extenuating circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and any other
information that would allow the Director to conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the
drilling permit, the applicant should retain the permit.
Natalie Menge
June 18, 2014
Page 2
Permit Fee & Notification
Payment was received in the amount of $100 via credit card. It is requested that notification be given
immediately upon the spudding of the well. This information should be relayed to the Oil & Gas Division,
Bismarck, via telephone. The following information must be included: Well name, legal location, permit number,
drilling contractor, company representative, date and time of spudding. Office hours are 8:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m.
and 1:00 p.m. to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a message if after hours
or on the weekend.
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey
contractor shall file a certified copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion.
Surveys must be submitted as one electronic copy, or in a form approved by the director. However, the director
may require the directional survey to be filed immediately after completion if the survey is needed to conduct the
operation of the director's office in a timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one adobe
document, with a certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve
(or when sliding) and 90 feet in the lateral.
Confidential status
Your request for confidential status of all information furnished to the Director, or his representatives, is
hereby granted. Such information, except production runs, shall remain confidential for six months commencing
on the date the well is spud.
Confidential status notwithstanding, the Director and his representatives shall have access to all well
records wherever located. Your company personnel, or any person performing work for your company shall
permit the Director and his representatives to come upon any lease, property, well, or drilling rig operated or
controlled by them, complying with all safety rules, and to inspect the records and operation of such wells and to
have access at all times to any and all records of wells. The Commission's field personnel periodically inspect
producing and drilling wells. Any information regarding such wells shall be made available to them at any time
upon request. The information so obtained by the field personnel shall be maintained in strict confidence and
shall be available only to the Commission and its staff.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12
hours, and tail cement utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi
before drilling the plug or initiating tests.
Logs NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and
porosity zones can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well bore, and
(3) a log from which the presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic cement evaluation
log) in every well in which production or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior to completing the well.
All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as one digital TIFF (tagged image file format) copy and one digital LAS (log
ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a standard CD, DVD, or attached to an email sent to
digitallogs@nd.gov Thank you for your cooperation.

David Burns
Engineering Technician

Surveys are required at least every 30 feet in the build section and every 90 feet in the lateral section of a horizontal well. Measurement
inaccuracies are not considered when determining compliance with the spacing/drilling unit boundary setback requirement except in the
following scenarios: 1) When the angle between the well bore and the respective boundary is 10 degrees or less; or 2) If Industry standard
methods and equipment are not utilized. Consult the applicable field order for exceptions.
If measurement inaccuracies are required to be considered, a 2° MWD measurement inaccuracy will be applied to the horizontal portion of the well
bore. This measurement inaccuracy is applied to the well bore from KOP to TD.

Engineering Technician
April 9, 2014
RE:
Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director
Marathon Oil Company

1.
BOP EQUIPMENT
Marathon Oil Company's minimum specifications for pressure
control equipment are as follows:
Ram Type:
13 5/8" 5000 psi blind, pipe and annular.
a. Due to Marathon's experience it is felt that the above
referenced BOP equipment is adequate for drilling this well.
The reduced permeability of the target zone along with
Marathon's area experience of drilling over 250 horizontal
wells indicate that a MASP of 3000 psi is more adjusted to
the reality of the reservoir.
BOP and other equipment testing:
a. Floor valve, dart valve, kill valves, check valve, manual
choke line valve, manual top drive valve, hydraulic top
drive valve, HCR, choke house valves, choke manifold,
choke hose, choke line, kill line, upper pipe rams, lower
pipe rams, blind rams (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min. High
Test: 5000 psi x 10 min.)
b. Annular Preventer (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min. High Test:
2500 psi x 10 min.)
c. Rotating head and Orbit Valve (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min.
High Test: 1500 psi x 10 min.)
Frequency:
a. After initial installation (NU BOPE).
b. Whenever any seal subject to test pressure is broken.
c. After any repairs compromising seal.
d. At 30-day intervals.
All other equipment (upper and lower Kelly cocks, IBOP,
etc) will be tested according to Onshore Oil and Gas
Order No. 2.

EVALUATION PROGRAM
The anticipated type and amount of testing, logging and coring
are as follows:
a. The logging program will consist of the following:
i. Waiver is attached not to run logs except those
shown below.

surface.

intermediate casing point.

below (base of Charles salt):
i. Samples will be obtained at 10' intervals to
intermediate casing point and at 30' intervals below
intermediate to TD.
c. No drill stem tests are anticipated.

5.
ABNORMAL PRESSURES AND H2S GAS
a. The maximum anticipated bottom-hole pressure is 7810 psi.
Abnormal pressures are not anticipated.
b. Potential exists for hydrogen sulfide gas in the Madison.
6.
Well Completion
a. A 4 ½" liner will be run from above the 7" casing shoe to
the bottom of the well.
Liner has frac sleeves
installed.
b. Tie back liner will be run from top of 4 ½" Liner back to
the surface.
c. Well will be fractured utilizing a 30 stage frac.
d. Pursuant to NDIC letter effective February 12,2014,
concerning Hydraulic Fracture Stimulation using Diesel
Fuels, Marathon Oil Company will not inject diesel fuel
or any diesel-type chemicals (68334-30-5, 68476-34-6,
68476-30-2, 68476-31-3, or 8008-20-6) during the
hydraulic fracture stimulation process or this well.
Marathon understands the guidelines that are outline in
the above referenced letter including the requirement to
obtain an Underground Injection Control, Class II permit
from the NDIC prior to commencing any Hydraulic Fracture
Stimulation in which any amount of diesel fuel or any
diesel type chemical is injected.
